<div id="review_3142713518" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3142713518" />
    <a title="Anoushka  Ghosh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41239985-anoushka-ghosh"><img alt="Anoushka  Ghosh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595741459p2/41239985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3142713518?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anoushka  Ghosh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anoushka  Ghosh" href="/user/show/41239985-anoushka-ghosh">Anoushka  Ghosh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3142713518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer221681127050963275">Brilliant. Brilliant. Brilliant.<br/><br/>Have I ever read a 23 volume manga within 3 days? No, I haven't. But do you know why it was possible? Because Fruits Basket is <i>breathtaking.</i> I haven't cried or hurt this much because of a manga before, I mean I have but come on, the emotional brilliance of this series is <b>U.n.d.e.n.i.a.b.l.e.</b><br/><br/>*****<br/><br/>I initially shipped Yuki and Tohru together. You know the obscure-unknown-girl-gets-with-popular-handsome-guy trope? Yeah, that's what I believed in. And I imagined that T</span>
  <span id="freeText221681127050963275" style="display:none">Brilliant. Brilliant. Brilliant.<br /><br />Have I ever read a 23 volume manga within 3 days? No, I haven't. But do you know why it was possible? Because Fruits Basket is <i>breathtaking.</i> I haven't cried or hurt this much because of a manga before, I mean I have but come on, the emotional brilliance of this series is <b>U.n.d.e.n.i.a.b.l.e.</b><br /><br />*****<br /><br />I initially shipped Yuki and Tohru together. You know the obscure-unknown-girl-gets-with-popular-handsome-guy trope? Yeah, that's what I believed in. And I imagined that Tohru would fall in love with Yuki, but Kyo would fall in love with Tohru and eventually get rejected by her. <i>Boy was I wrong.</i><br /><br />I think I broke a little inside when I came to understand Yuki's story and his <i>utter isolation</i> from society and his innocent jealousy of Kyo's friendship with other kids. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The sheer irony of him carrying Kyo's cap on his head all this time is metaphorical and when he wants to give it back to Kyo, all he gets is rage and complete rejection. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Which I believe is very important theme in Fruits Basket, <i>ostracisation</i> that is. <i>Akito, Yuki, Kyo, Kisa, Momiji, Hanajima, Kureno, Ren, .</i>All of them endured hate and most notably: loneliness.<br /><br />And Tohru comes in like a beacon of hope, kindness, and <i>so much warmth</i>. Her character symbolises all the good things in the world even when it seems like the world is hopeless. Eventually I like Kyo and Tohru together too because 1) him getting all flustered by how cute she is is <b>
  <i>THE CUTEST THING</i>
</b> ever; 2) The way they complement each other and lastly, how <i>she accepts him for all he is: the good and the bad.</i> <br /><br />*****<br /><br /><i>"It's frightening that there's no guarantee that I'll be loved."</i><br /><br />The way the author turned around Akito's character was pure ingenuity. At first, I believed that I would never forgive Akito's character for all the wrong <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[she (yes she!) had ever done. I thought that she would remain the <i>big, bad villain</i> for a long time. And then came Tohru, who touched Akito's dark heart and showed her the power of a kind word. I think I cried a bottle of tears when they all lost their bonds with Akito. The sheer selflessness of Akito in the last few chapters, catalysed by the idea that "I want to live a life devoid of long-established bonds," really turned Akito into a character I admire. And man, Shigure <i>oof.</i> Their relationship is so wholesome because Akito <i>finally</i> understands that she's not alone, and she's capable of being loved. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Which brings me to the part that the psychological torture that Akito put a few of the Zodiac animals through is not easily forgiven; but the grace with which the 12 take it is a testament to the fact that forgiveness is <i>much</i> better than revenge.<br /><br />*****<br /><br />Just to put out some unpopular opinions, my favourite couple is still <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Yuki and Machi, so much so that I wish I saw their epilogue as well. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The way Yuki transforms from a guy with the least self confidence and a person who thought he was not capable of making friends, to a person who falls in love with a girl and makes her realise what a beautiful person he is, is incredible. It's a good time to mention that Kakeru Nanabe is a human being who makes me smile because I think <i>he</i> in some way contributed to Yuki's Metamorphosis and it makes me so happy. I know I am in the minority here, but as you can clearly make out: my favourite boy is Sohma Yuki. And well Momiji, obviously; <b>HOW CAN YOU NOT LOVE HIM.</b><br /><br /><i>"I love you. When did I start to love you so much?”</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="221681127050963275" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3327707131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1433256842793956106">I thoroughly enjoyed this entire collection. It gave me all of the emotions from heartbreak to bubbly happiness. I will say that since it is a manga, that some of the sexual themes throughout it were not for me - the pedophile jokes for instance or the sex toys & fetishes - but these were not super prevalent so I was able to overlook them for the most part and it seems to be an issue in most manga of this subtype. Instead I choose to focus on the dysfunctional familial aspects. Everything from a</span>
  <span id="freeText1433256842793956106" style="display:none">I thoroughly enjoyed this entire collection. It gave me all of the emotions from heartbreak to bubbly happiness. I will say that since it is a manga, that some of the sexual themes throughout it were not for me - the pedophile jokes for instance or the sex toys &amp; fetishes - but these were not super prevalent so I was able to overlook them for the most part and it seems to be an issue in most manga of this subtype. Instead I choose to focus on the dysfunctional familial aspects. Everything from abuse to found family is explored. The romance was such a slow, steady burn too. I was here for all of the relationships that were explored and not just the three main characters'. I think this story of how love and friendship can be a light during darkness and depression was such a good message throughout the entire story. Accepting others as they are is another theme I recognized and enjoyed. I think that some of the "fluidness" of genders in the characters was also done well, in my opinion as a straight female. (If I am wrong, please correct me.) I did think some chapters were "filler" and not always entertaining. I also feel like the ending was stretched out for too long, for no apparent reason. Overall, this was a fun story with a cast of characters I will treasure always. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1433256842793956106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12195565660598937013">My first manga and my favorite series of all time, to date. I completed Fruits Basket back in 2009, and for the last decade have re-read the series for analyzation, reflection, and most often, pure enjoyment. <br/><br/>The manga itself revolves around Tohru Honda, a recently orphaned high highschooler, who after meeting Shigure, Yuki and Kyo Sohma, learns that 12 members of the Sohma family are possessed by the animals of the Chinese zodiac. The series follows Tohru has she progresses through high school </span>
  <span id="freeText12195565660598937013" style="display:none">My first manga and my favorite series of all time, to date. I completed Fruits Basket back in 2009, and for the last decade have re-read the series for analyzation, reflection, and most often, pure enjoyment. <br /><br />The manga itself revolves around Tohru Honda, a recently orphaned high highschooler, who after meeting Shigure, Yuki and Kyo Sohma, learns that 12 members of the Sohma family are possessed by the animals of the Chinese zodiac. The series follows Tohru has she progresses through high school with the Sohma family, helping to heal their past (and current) emotional hurt, trying to break their family curse, and learning more about herself and where she fits in with the Sohma's. <br /><br />I highly recommend this manga to anyone looking for a romcom with an unexpected twist, especially for those watching the new 2019 anime adaptation. It's a timeless series that fans old and new will enjoy for years to come. <br /><br />Note: The English romanization of character names are different in the Japanese version, which might lead to some confusion with the newer serializations and the anime. Example:<br />Tohru Honda - Tōru Honda<br />Yuki Sohma - Yuki Sōma</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2317549903633161822"><b>Name (in native language) :</b> <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18983717._' rel='nofollow noopener'>高屋奈月</a><br/><br/>Natsuki Takaya (高屋 奈月 Takaya Natsuki, real name Naka Hatake) is the penname of a Japanese manga artist best-known for creating the series Fruits Basket. She was born on July 7, 1973; (Tanabata). Takaya is left-handed and once revealed that she wanted to be a mangaka since first grade, when her sister started drawing. <br/><br/>She was born in Shizuoka, Japan, but was raised i</span>
  <span id="freeText2317549903633161822" style="display:none"><b>Name (in native language) :</b> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18983717._" rel="nofollow noopener">高屋奈月</a><br /><br />Natsuki Takaya (高屋 奈月 Takaya Natsuki, real name Naka Hatake) is the penname of a Japanese manga artist best-known for creating the series Fruits Basket. She was born on July 7, 1973; (Tanabata). Takaya is left-handed and once revealed that she wanted to be a mangaka since first grade, when her sister started drawing. <br /><br />She was born in Shizuoka, Japan, but was raised in Tokyo, where she made her debut in 1992. She enjoys video games such as the Final Fantasy series or Sakura Wars, or working on her different manga series, such as Fruits Basket, which is the second best-selling shōjo manga ever in Japan, and the top selling shōjo manga in North America. Fruits Basket has also been adapted into a twenty-six-episode anime series. <br /><br />In 2001, Takaya received a Kodansha Manga Award for shōjo manga for Fruits Basket.<br /><br />According to Takaya (in a sidebar of a Fruits Basket manga volume), she enjoys drawing girls (girly ones) more than she does boys. Takaya also enjoys electronics and music, but dislikes talking about herself. Also revealed in a sidebar of Fruits Basket, Takaya broke her drawing arm (left) after Fruits Basket volume six was published. She had to go into surgery, and as a result, had put Fruits Basket on a brief hiatus. Takaya made a full recovery, but complains that her handwriting had gotten uglier, due to the surgery. During her hospital stay, she gained an interest in baseball.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2317549903633161822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
